---

**Sourcegraph Repositories:** `github.com/sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6`, `github.com/sg-evals/istio--2300e245`, `github.com/sg-evals/emissary--3bbdbe0f`

Find all concrete server implementations of the `AggregatedDiscoveryServiceServer` gRPC interface across xDS control plane repositories.

## Background

The Aggregated Discovery Service (ADS) is the primary xDS protocol for delivering configuration to Envoy proxies. The gRPC service is defined in the proto file `envoy/service/discovery/v3/ads.proto`:

```protobuf
service AggregatedDiscoveryService {
  rpc StreamAggregatedResources(stream DiscoveryRequest)
    returns (stream DiscoveryResponse) {}

  rpc DeltaAggregatedResources(stream DeltaDiscoveryRequest)
    returns (stream DeltaDiscoveryResponse) {}
}
```

When compiled to Go, this generates a server interface `AggregatedDiscoveryServiceServer` in the package `github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/service/discovery/v3`. Any struct that implements the methods of this interface acts as an xDS control plane server.

## Repositories

Three repositories are available under `/workspace/`:

- `/workspace/go-control-plane/` — envoyproxy/go-control-plane (Go xDS server SDK, reference implementations)
- `/workspace/istio/` — istio/istio (Istio control plane with Pilot xDS server)
- `/workspace/emissary/` — emissary-ingress/emissary (Envoy-based API gateway with xDS configuration server)

## Task

Find **all struct types** that implement the `AggregatedDiscoveryServiceServer` interface across all three repositories. These are types that provide concrete implementations of:
- `StreamAggregatedResources(stream AggregatedDiscoveryService_StreamAggregatedResourcesServer) error`
- `DeltaAggregatedResources(stream AggregatedDiscoveryService_DeltaAggregatedResourcesServer) error`

For each implementor, record:
- `repo`: one of `envoyproxy/go-control-plane`, `istio/istio`, or `emissary-ingress/emissary`
- `file`: path relative to the repository root (e.g., `pkg/server/v3/server.go`)
- `struct_name`: the name of the struct type that implements the interface (e.g., `Server`, `DiscoveryServer`)

## Output

Write your results to `/workspace/implementors.json` as a JSON array:

```json
[
  {
    "repo": "envoyproxy/go-control-plane",
    "file": "pkg/server/v3/server.go",
    "struct_name": "Server"
  },
  {
    "repo": "istio/istio",
    "file": "pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go",
    "struct_name": "DiscoveryServer"
  }
]
```

## Inclusion Criteria

**Include:**
- Production server implementations (the main control plane servers)
- Test server implementations (mock servers, fake servers for testing)
- Partial implementations (types that implement at least one of the two methods)
- Embedded server types (if a struct embeds the interface but provides its own methods)

**Exclude:**
- The generated protobuf interface definition itself (in `*_grpc.pb.go` files)
- Pure interface embeddings without method implementations (e.g., `type X struct { AggregatedDiscoveryServiceServer }` with no methods)
- Deprecated or commented-out implementations
- Vendor directory code
- Types that only **call** the server interface (clients), not implement it

This ensures that we do not\\n267: // block forever on\\n268: func (con *ProxyConnection) sendRequest(req *discovery.DiscoveryRequest) {\\n269: \\tcon.requestsChan.Put(req)\\n270: }\\n271: \\n272: func (con *ProxyConnection) isClosed() bool {\\n273: \\tselect {\\n274: \\tcase <-con.stopChan:\\n275: \\t\\treturn true\\n276: \\tdefault:\\n277: \\t\\treturn false\\n278: \\t}\\n279: }\\n280: \\n281: type adsStream interface {\\n282: \\tSend(*discovery.DiscoveryResponse) error\\n283: \\tRecv() (*discovery.DiscoveryRequest, error)\\n284: \\tContext() context.Context\\n285: }\\n286: \\n287: // StreamAggregatedResources is an implementation of XDS API used for proxying between Istiod and Envoy.\\n288: // Every time envoy makes a fresh connection to the agent, we reestablish a new connection to the upstream xds\\n289: // This ensures that a new connection between istiod and agent doesn't end up consuming pending messages from envoy\\n290: // as the new connection may not go to the same istiod. Vice versa case also applies.\\n291: func (p *XdsProxy) StreamAggregatedResources(downstream DiscoveryStream) error {\\n292: \\tproxyLog.Debugf(\\\"accepted XDS connection from Envoy, forwarding to upstream XDS server\\\")\\n293: \\treturn p.handleStream(downstream)\\n294: }\\n295: \\n296: func (p *XdsProxy) handleStream(downstream adsStream) error {\\n297: \\tcon := &ProxyConnection{\\n298: \\t\\tconID:           connectionNumber.Inc(),\\n299: \\t\\tupstreamError:   make(chan error), // can be produced by recv and send\\n300: \\t\\tdownstreamError: make(chan error), // can be produced by recv and send\\n301: \\t\\t// Requests channel is unbounded. The Envoy<->XDS Proxy<->Istiod system produces a natural\\n302: \\t\\t// looping of Recv and Send. Due to backpressure introduced by gRPC natively (that is, Send() can\\n303: \\t\\t// only send so much data without being Recv'd before it starts blocking), along with the\\n304: \\t\\t// backpressure provided by our channels, we have a risk of deadlock where both Xdsproxy and\\n305: \\t\\t// Istiod are trying to Send, but both are blocked by gRPC backpressure until Recv() is called.\\n306: \\t\\t// However, Recv can fail to be called by Send being blocked. This can be triggered by the two\\n307: \\t\\t// sources in our system (Envoy request and Istiod pushes) producing more events than we can keep\\n308: \\t\\t// up with.\\n309: \\t\\t// See https://github.com/istio/istio/issues/39209 for more information\\n310: \\t\\t//\\n311: \\t\\t// To prevent these issues, we need to either:\\n312: \\t\\t// 1. Apply backpressure directly to Envoy requests or Istiod pushes\\n313: \\t\\t// 2. Make part of the system unbounded\\n314: \\t\\t//\\n315: \\t\\t// (1) is challenging because we cannot do a conditional Recv (for Envoy requests), and changing\\n316: \\t\\t// the control plane requires substantial changes. Instead, we make the requests channel\\n317: \\t\\t// unbounded. This is the least likely to cause issues as the messages we store here are the\\n318: \\t\\t// smallest relative to other channels.\\n319: \\t\\trequestsChan: channels.NewUnbounded[*discovery.DiscoveryRequest](),\\n320: \\t\\t// Allow a buffer of 1. This ensures we queue up at most 2 (one in process, 1 pending) responses before forwarding.\\n321: \\t\\tresponsesChan: make(chan *discovery.DiscoveryResponse, 1),\\n322: \\t\\tstopChan:      make(chan struct{}),\\n323: \\t\\tdownstream:    downstream,\\n324: \\t}\\n325: \\n326: \\tp.registerStream(con)\\n327: \\tdefer p.unregisterStream(con)\\n328: \\n329: \\tctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(context.Background(), time.Second*5)\\n330: \\tdefer cancel()\\n331: \\n332: \\tupstreamConn, err := p.buildUpstreamConn(ctx)\\n333: \\tif err != nil {\\n334: \\t\\tproxyLog.Errorf(\\\"failed to connect to upstream %s: %v\\\", p.istiodAddress, err)\\n335: \\t\\tmetrics.IstiodConnectionFailures.Increment()\\n336: \\t\\treturn err\\n337: \\t}\\n338: \\tdefer upstreamConn.Close()\\n339: \\n340: \\txds := discovery.NewAggregatedDiscoveryServiceClient(upstreamConn)\\n341: \\tctx = metadata.AppendToOutgoingContext(context.Background(), \\\"ClusterID\\\", p.clusterID)\\n342: \\tfor k, v := range p.xdsHeaders {\\n343: \\t\\tctx = metadata.AppendToOutgoingContext(ctx, k, v)\\n344: \\t}\\n345: \\t// We must propagate upstream termination to Envoy. }\\n355: \\n356: func (p *XdsProxy) handleUpstream(ctx context.Context, con *ProxyConnection, xds discovery.AggregatedDiscoveryServiceClient) error {\\n357: \\tlog := proxyLog.WithLabels(\\\"id\\\", Vice versa case also applies.\n291: func (p *XdsProxy) StreamAggregatedResources(downstream DiscoveryStream) error {\n292: \tproxyLog.Debugf(\"accepted XDS connection from Envoy, forwarding to upstream XDS server\")\n293: \treturn p.handleStream(downstream)\n294: }\n295: \n296: func (p *XdsProxy) handleStream(downstream adsStream) error {\n297: \tcon := &ProxyConnection{\n298: \t\tconID:           connectionNumber.Inc(),\n299: \t\tupstreamError:   make(chan error), // can be produced by recv and send\n300: \t\tdownstreamError: make(chan error), // can be produced by recv and send\n301: \t\t// Requests channel is unbounded. The Envoy<->XDS Proxy<->Istiod system produces a natural\n302: \t\t// looping of Recv and Send. Due to backpressure introduced by gRPC natively (that is, Send() can\n303: \t\t// only send so much data without being Recv'd before it starts blocking), along with the\n304: \t\t// backpressure provided by our channels, we have a risk of deadlock where both Xdsproxy and\n305: \t\t// Istiod are trying to Send, but both are blocked by gRPC backpressure until Recv() is called.\n306: \t\t// However, Recv can fail to be called by Send being blocked. This can be triggered by the two\n307: \t\t// sources in our system (Envoy request and Istiod pushes) producing more events than we can keep\n308: \t\t// up with.\n309: \t\t// See https://github.com/istio/istio/issues/39209 for more information\n310: \t\t//\n311: \t\t// To prevent these issues, we need to either:\n312: \t\t// 1. Apply backpressure directly to Envoy requests or Istiod pushes\n313: \t\t// 2. Make part of the system unbounded\n314: \t\t//\n315: \t\t// (1) is challenging because we cannot do a conditional Recv (for Envoy requests), and changing\n316: \t\t// the control plane requires substantial changes. Instead, we make the requests channel\n317: \t\t// unbounded. This is the least likely to cause issues as the messages we store here are the\n318: \t\t// smallest relative to other channels.\n319: \t\trequestsChan: channels.NewUnbounded[*discovery.DiscoveryRequest](),\n320: \t\t// Allow a buffer of 1. This ensures we queue up at most 2 (one in process, 1 pending) responses before forwarding.\n321: \t\tresponsesChan: make(chan *discovery.DiscoveryResponse, 1),\n322: \t\tstopChan:      make(chan struct{}),\n323: \t\tdownstream:    downstream,\n324: \t}\n325: \n326: \tp.registerStream(con)\n327: \tdefer p.unregisterStream(con)\n328: \n329: \tctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(context.Background(), time.Second*5)\n330: \tdefer cancel()\n331: \n332: \tupstreamConn, err := p.buildUpstreamConn(ctx)\n333: \tif err != nil {\n334: \t\tproxyLog.Errorf(\"failed to connect to upstream %s: %v\", p.istiodAddress, err)\n335: \t\tmetrics.IstiodConnectionFailures.Increment()\n336: \t\treturn err\n337: \t}\n338: \tdefer upstreamConn.Close()\n339: \n340: \txds := discovery.NewAggregatedDiscoveryServiceClient(upstreamConn)\n341: \tctx = metadata.AppendToOutgoingContext(context.Background(), \"ClusterID\", p.clusterID)\n342: \tfor k, v := range p.xdsHeaders {\n343: \t\tctx = metadata.AppendToOutgoingContext(ctx, k, v)\n344: \t}\n345: \t// We must propagate upstream termination to Envoy. This ensures that we resume the full XDS sequence on new connection\n346: \treturn p.handleUpstream(ctx, con, xds)\n347: }\n348: \n349: func (p *XdsProxy) buildUpstreamConn(ctx context.Context) (*grpc.ClientConn, error) {\n350: \tp.optsMutex.RLock()\n351: \topts := p.dialOptions\n352: \tp.optsMutex.RUnlock()\n353: \treturn grpc.DialContext(ctx, p.istiodAddress, opts...)\n354: }\n355: \n356: func (p *XdsProxy) handleUpstream(ctx context.Context, con *ProxyConnection, xds discovery.AggregatedDiscoveryServiceClient) error {\n357: \tlog := proxyLog.WithLabels(\"id\", con.conID)\n358: \tupstream, err := xds.StreamAggregatedResources(ctx,\n359: \t\tgrpc.MaxCallRecvMsgSize(defaultClientMaxReceiveMessageSize))\n360: \tif err != nil {\n361: \t\t// Envoy logs errors again, so no need to assistance\n28:  *     of the methods in a callback object.\n29:  * - Once the Server is running, Envoy can open a gRPC stream to it.\n30:  *   - On connection, Envoy will get handed the most recent During\\n191: \\t\\t// loading request, concurrency=1. Once that request is done, concurrency is enabled.\\n192: \\t\\t// However, the XDS stream is long lived, so the first request would block all others. As a\\n193: \\t\\t// result, we should exit the first request immediately; clients will retry.\\n194: \\t\\tfirstRequest.Store(false)\\n195: \\t\\treturn status.Error(codes.Unavailable, \\\"server warmup not complete; try again\\\")\\n196: \\t}\\n197: \\t// Check if server is ready to accept clients and process new requests.\\n198: \\t// Currently ready means caches have been synced and hence can build\\n199: \\t// clusters correctly. Without this check, InitContext() call below would\\n200: \\t// initialize with empty config, leading to reconnected Envoys losing\\n201: \\t// configuration. This is an additional safety check inaddition to adding\\n202: \\t// cachesSynced logic to readiness probe to handle cases where kube-proxy\\n203: \\t// ip tables update latencies.\\n204: \\t// See https://github.com/istio/istio/issues/25495.\\n205: \\tif !s.IsServerReady() {\\n206: \\t\\treturn status.Error(codes.Unavailable, \\\"server is not ready to serve discovery information\\\")\\n207: \\t}\\n208: \\n209: \\tctx := stream.Context()\\n210: \\tpeerAddr := \\\"0.0.0.0\\\"\\n211: \\tif peerInfo, ok := peer.FromContext(ctx);
